Selling a Slave Girl Excluding Her Pregnancy: A Principle of Valid Exception
Ruling on sale with exception of pregnancy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on excepting an inseparable part from a sale and apply the Hanafi principle that only independently contractible items can be excepted.

Core Idea
An exception of something that cannot be sold alone invalidates the entire contract.

This lesson examines a specific case in sales (buyu') where a seller attempts to sell a slave girl but excludes her pregnancy. The Hanafi ruling is that such a sale is void (fasid) because the pregnancy cannot be the subject of an independent contract. The underlying principle is that exception (istithna') is only valid if the excepted part can itself be sold separately. We will explore this principle and its implications.

Guided Path
1
State the case
A seller sells a slave girl but excepts her pregnancy (istithna' al-haml).
2
Identify the ruling
The sale is void (fasid) according to the Hanafi school.
Fasid means the contract is corrupt and not legally effective.
3
Recognize the underlying principle
The author states the principle: 'Whatever is not valid to be isolated in a contract is not valid to be excepted from it.'
This is a general rule in Hanafi sales law.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Pregnancy (haml) cannot be sold or owned independently because it is not a separate property with an independent value. Therefore, its exception is invalid, and since the contract contains a condition that is impossible to fulfill, the entire sale is corrupted.
Compare with exceptions like a limb or specific item that can be sold separately.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school may consider the sale valid with the exception being ineffective, but the sale of the slave without the pregnancy remains valid if the price is apportioned.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باندی بیچی مگر اس کے حمل کا استثناء کر لیا تو بیع فاسد ہے
قال ومن اشترى جارية الاحملها فالبيع فاسد و الاصل ان مالا يصح افراده بالعقد لا يصح استثناؤه من العقد
A slave girl was sold but the seller excepted her pregnancy, so the sale is void. He said: Whoever buys a slave girl except her pregnancy, the sale is void, and the principle is that whatever is not valid to be isolated in a contract is not valid to be excepted from it.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a concise ruling: selling a slave girl with an exception of her pregnancy renders the sale void. The principle is that anything which itself cannot be made the subject of an independent contract (e.g., a pregnancy cannot be sold separately as it is not a distinct property with an independent value) cannot be validly excepted from a contract. The exception is ineffective, and since it is a condition that cannot be fulfilled, the sale as a whole is corrupted.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): Excluding a part from the sold item.
حمل (haml): Pregnancy of an animal or slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling a slave girl with the exception of her pregnancy?
A) The sale is valid, and the pregnancy remains with the seller.
B) The sale is void.
C) The sale is valid if the buyer agrees.
D) The sale is suspended until delivery.

Key Takeaway
A sale is void if the seller excepts a part that cannot be sold independently, such as pregnancy, because the condition is invalid and corrupts the contract.

Sale of 'Ayn with Deferred Delivery: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on sale with deferred delivery of 'ayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale of a specific existing item ('ayn) with a deferred delivery condition, explain the reasoning (qiyas khafi) that deferment is only suitable for debts, and identify the exception for salam contracts.

Core Idea
Deferring delivery of a specific existing item is invalid because it imposes an unnecessary condition on what is already present.

Imagine buying a specific cow but the seller says 'I will deliver it in one month'. Is this permissible? In the Hanafi school, such a condition renders the sale invalid (fasid) because deferment (ajal) is meant to ease acquisition of non-existent items (debts), not goods already in hand. This ruling reflects a key principle: conditions inconsistent with the nature of the contract invalidate it. However, an important exception is the salam contract, where deferment is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale of a specific existing item ('ayn) with a condition that delivery be deferred until a future time (e.g., beginning of the month). According to the Hanafi school, the ruling is that the sale is fasid (invalid).
The condition is called 'shart fasid' (invalid condition).
2
Understand the proof (qiyas khafi)
The proof is based on qiyas: deferment (ajal) was legislated to provide ease (tarfehi) and is therefore suitable for debts (dayn), which are not present and need time to acquire. 'Ayn (specific goods) already exist, so a deferment condition is superfluous and changes the nature of the contract. This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because it derives the ruling from the wisdom behind the legislation of ajal.
The source mentions that dirhams and dinars are considered as dayn in this context.
3
Note the exception: salam contract
The author of al-Hidayah adds the word 'fi' (in) to the general statement to exclude salam. In salam, the subject matter (muslam fih) is a deferred obligation (dayn) on the seller, not an existing 'ayn. Therefore, deferment is suitable and the contract is valid.
This shows that the ruling is specific to sales of existing goods (excluding salam).
4
Consider cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school allows deferment in sale of 'ayn if both parties agree, viewing the condition as valid. The Hanafi school considers it fasid because the condition contradicts the immediate nature of the sale.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن باع عينا على ان لا يسلمه الى رأس الشهر فالبيع فاسد لان الاجل في البيع العين باطل فيكون شرطا فاسدا وهذا لان الاجل شرع ترفيها فيليق بالديون دون الاعيان ترجمہ کہا اور اگر کسی نے عین شئی اس شرط پر فروخت کی کہ وہ اس کو چاند رات تک سپر نہیں کرے گا تو بیع فاسد ہے کیونکہ مبیع عین میں میعاد باطل ہے لہذا یہ شرط فاسد ہوگی کیونکہ میعاد آسانی کے لئے مشروع ہوتی ہے پس یہ دیون کے لائق ہے نہ کہ اعیان کے۔ تشریح مسئلہ اگر کسی نے مال عین یعنی در اہم ود نائیر کے علاوہ کسی متعینہ چیز کو اس شرط کے ساتھ فروخت کیا کہ مبیع پہلی تاریخ کو یا آخری تاریخ کو سپر دکروں گا تو یہ بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہلت اور میعاد آسانی کے لئے مشروع ہوئی ہے یعنی میعاد اس لئے مشروع کی گئی ہے تا کہ اس مدت میں اس شئی کا حاصل کرنا آسان ہو جائے جس کے بارے میں میعاد مقرر کی گئی پس میعاد دیون یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر کے مناسب ہے اعیان کے مناسب نہیں ہے کیونکہ مال عین تو بالفعل موجود ہوتا ہے اور دراہم ودنا نیر آہستہ آہستہ تلاش کئے جاتے ہیں پس جو چیز بالفعل موجود ہے اس میں میعاد کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ورنہ خواہ مخواہ تحصیل حاصل کا مرتکب ہونا پڑے گا ہاں جو چیز بالفعل موجود نہیں ہے اس میں میعاد اور مہلت دینا مفید اور کارآمد ہے۔ پس جب میعاد اعیان کے مناسب نہیں ہے تو سبیع عین یعنی معینہ موجودہ بیع میں اجل اور میعاد کا ذکر کرنا باطل ہوگا اور میعاد کی شرط لگانا شرط فاسد ہوگا اور شرط فاسد سے چونکہ بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے شرط کے ساتھ بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے بیچ کے بعد لفظ مین بڑھا کر مسلم فیہ کو خارج کر دیا ہے کیونکہ بیع سلم میں مسلم فیہ صبیح تو ہوتی ہے مگر عین نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ میں واجب ہوتی ہے اور اس کی سپردگی ایک مدت کے بعد ہوتی ہے اس لئے مسلم فیہ کے لئے اجل اور میعاد ناسب ہے۔
He said: And whoever sells a specific thing on the condition that he will not deliver it until the beginning of the month, the sale is invalid (fasid) because deferment in the sale of a specific thing is invalid, so it is an invalid condition. And this is because deferment is legislated for ease, so it is suitable for debts, not for specific goods. Commentary: If someone sells a specific property, i.e., a specific thing other than dirhams and dinars, with the condition that he will deliver the sold item at the beginning or end of the month, then this sale is invalid. The proof is that respite and deferment are legislated for ease, i.e., deferment is legislated so that during that period obtaining the thing for which the deferment is set becomes easier. So deferment is suitable for debts, i.e., dirhams and dinars, not for specific goods, because a specific good is already present, while dirhams and dinars are sought gradually. Therefore, for something that is already present, there is little need for deferment; otherwise, one would unnecessarily be engaged in obtaining what is already obtained. Yes, for something not already present, giving deferment and respite is beneficial and effective. So when deferment is not suitable for specific goods, mentioning a term in a sale of a specific existing thing is invalid, and stipulating a term is an invalid condition, and since an invalid condition makes the sale invalid, the sale with that condition is invalid. The author of al-Hidayah inserted the word 'fi' [meaning 'in'] after 'sale' to exclude salam, because in a salam sale, the subject matter (muslam fih) is specified but not a specific existing thing; rather, it is an obligation on the seller's liability, and its delivery is after a period; hence deferment is suitable for muslam fih.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a sale of a specific existing item ('ayn) with a condition that delivery be deferred until a certain time, such as the beginning of the month. The ruling is that such a sale is fasid (invalid) because the condition of deferment is invalid for 'ayn property. The reasoning is that deferment (ajal) was legislated to provide ease (tarfehi), and it is appropriate for debts (dayn) — which are not physically present and need time to be acquired — not for specific existing goods ('ayn) that are already present and can be delivered immediately. The author then clarifies that this rule applies to all 'ayn property other than dirhams and dinars (which are considered as debts in many contexts). The commentary also notes a refinement by the author of al-Hidayah: he added the word 'فى' (in) after 'باع' to exclude salam contracts, because in salam, the subject matter (muslam fih) is a specified liability (dayn) on the seller, not a specific existing item; hence deferment is suitable. Thus, the ruling does not apply to salam. This passage is from the Hanafi school and reflects the principle that conditions inconsistent with the nature of the contract (muqtada al-'aqd) render the contract fasid if they are not customary or legally permitted.

Key Terms
اجل (ajal): Deferment or term specified for payment or delivery in a contract.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is legally invalid and disrupts the contract, leading to the contract being fasid in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is valid because the condition is agreed upon.
B) The sale is fasid because deferment is invalid for 'ayn property.
C) The sale is batil because the subject matter is not delivered immediately.
D) The sale is valid if the buyer pays in advance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, deferring delivery in a sale of a specific existing item ('ayn) renders the contract fasid because ajal is legislated for debts, not for goods already in hand; the condition of deferment is an invalid condition that nullifies the contract.

Excluding Unborn Child from Sale of Slave-Girl
Ruling on selling a slave-girl while excluding her unborn child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an unborn child is excepted from a slave-girl sale, apply the principle that inseparable parts cannot be excepted, and distinguish between contracts nullified by invalid conditions versus those that are not.

Core Idea
If a part cannot be sold alone, it cannot be validly excepted from a sale; the exception nullifies commutative contracts.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines what happens when a seller tries to exclude the unborn child (haml) from a slave-girl sale. The Hanafi ruling is that the sale becomes fasid because the exception is invalid. The underlying principle is that anything that cannot be independently contracted cannot be validly excepted. The text then expands to other contracts, distinguishing between commutative (mu'awada) and non-commutative contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and the principle
Identify the hukm: sale of slave-girl with exception of unborn child is fasid. The principle: whatever cannot be contracted alone cannot be excepted.
The exception becomes an invalid condition.
2
Identify why the unborn child cannot be excepted
The unborn child is legally like a limb (bimanzilat al-atraf) because it is physically attached. Just as limbs cannot be sold separately, the child cannot be excepted.
This is the core of the qiyas reasoning.
3
Recognize the classification of contracts
The text divides contracts into three types: (1) both contract and exception fasid (commutative: sale, ijarah, kitabah, rahn), (2) contract valid, exception void (non-commutative: hibah, sadaqah, nikah, khul', sulh), (3) both valid (wasiyyah due to inheritance analogy).
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Shafi'i holds the exception is valid and the sale is sound. This ikhtilaf stems from different classifications of the unborn child and the effect of conditions.
Hanafi: invalid condition nullifies commutative contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن اشترى جارية الاحملها فالبيع فاسد و الاصل ان مالا يصح افراده بالعقد لا يصح استثناؤه من العقد والحمل من هذا القبيل وهذا لانه بمنزلة اطراف الحيوان لاتصاله به خلقة وبيع الاصل يتناولها فالا ستثناء يكون على خلاف الموجب فلم يصح فيصير شرطا فاسدا والبيع يبطل به والكتابة والاجارة والرهن بمنزلة البيع لانها تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة غيران المفسد فى الكتابة ما يتمكن في صلب، العقد منها والهبة والصدقة والنكاح والخلع والصلح عن دم العمد لا تبطل باستثناء الحمل بل يبطل الاستثناء لان هذه العقود لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة وكذا الوصية لا تبطل به لكن يصح الاستثناء حتى يكون الحمل مير اثار الجارية وصية لان الوصية اخت الميراث والميراث يجرى فيما فى البطن بخلاف ما اذا استثنى خدمتها لان الميراث لا يجرى فيها ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے باندی خریدی علاوہ اس کے حمل کے تو بیع فاسد ہے اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کا تنہا عقد کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے اس کا عقد سے استثناء کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اور حمل اسی قسم سے ہے اور اس لئے کہ حمل، حیوان کے اطراف کے مرتبہ میں ہے کیونکہ حمل مبیع کے ساتھ پیدائشی طور پر متصل ہے اور اصلی کی بیچ اطراف کو شامل ہوتی ہے اس لئے استثناء کرنا موجب عقد کے خلاف ہوگا پس استثنا صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ اور استثناء ایک شرط فاسد ہو جائے گا اور بیج اس کی وجہ سے باطل ہو جائے گی اور کتابت اجارہ اور رہن بیچ کے مرتبہ میں ہیں کیونکہ یہ عقود بھی فاسد شرطوں سے باطل ہو جاتے ہیں۔ مگر کتابت کو فاسد کرنے والی وہ شرط ہے جو عقد کی قیمت کی ذات میں ہو۔ اور ہبہ ، صدقہ ، نکاح ضلع اور صلح عن دم العمد حمل کے استثناء سے باطل نہیں ہوتے ہیں بلکہ استثناء باطل ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ یہ عقود شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ اور اسی طرح وصیت بھی حمل کا استثناء کرنے سے باطل نہ ہوگی لیکن استثناء صحیح ہو جائے گا حتی کہ حمل میراث ہوگا اور باندی وصیت ہوگی کیونکہ وصیت میراث کی بہن ہے اور میراث ایسی چیز میں جاری ہو جاتی ہے جو پیٹ میں ہو ۔ برخلاف اس کے جبکہ اس کی خدمت کا استثناء کیا ہو کیونکہ خدمت میں میراث جاری نہیں ہوتی۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے باندی خریدی لیکن اس کے حمل کا استثناء کیا تو یہ بیچ فاسد ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کی تفصیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ وہ عقد جس میں استثناء کیا گیا ہو اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں، (۱) وہ جس میں عقد اور استثناء دونوں فاسد ہو جاتے ہیں۔ (۲ وہ جس میں عقد مسیح ہوتا ہے اور استثناء باطل ہوتا ہے۔ (۳) وہ جس میں عقد اور استثنا دونوں صحیح ہو جاتے ہیں ۔ قسم اول جیسے بیج اجارہ کتابت اور رہن مثلا کسی نے اپنی باندی فروخت کی لیکن اس کا عمل فروخت نہیں کیا یا اپنا مکان کرایہ پر دیا اور اس کا کرایہ باندی کو قرار دیا مگر اس کا حمل کرایہ میں شامل نہیں کیا یا اپنی باندی کو کسی کے پاس رہن رکھا مگر اس کا حمل رہن نہیں رکھا گیا۔ یا اپنا غلام مکاتب بنایا اور بدل کتابت باندی مقرر کی گئی مگر اس کا حمل بدل کتابت میں شامل نہیں کیا گیا ان تمام صورتوں میں بیج فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ یہ عقود شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتے ہیں اور یہ عقود، شروط فاسدہ سے اس لئے باطل ہو جاتے ہیں کہ بیچ کے علاوہ یعنی اجارہ ، کتابت اور رہن مینوں عقد معاوضہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بیج کے معنی میں ہیں۔ اور بیع شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے ۔ جیسا کہ سابق میں بیان ہوا اس لئے جو عقود بیع کے معنی میں ہیں وہ بھی شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جائیں گے اور استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے اور جس
He said: And whoever buys a slave-girl except her unborn child, the sale is fasid. The principle is that whatever cannot be validly contracted alone cannot be validly excepted from a contract. The unborn child is of this category. This is because it is like the limbs of the animal due to its creation-based attachment to it. The sale of the principal includes it. So the exception is contrary to the requirement [of the contract] and is thus invalid. It becomes an invalid condition, and the sale is nullified by it. Kitabah, ijarah, and rahn are like sale because they are nullified by invalid conditions, except that what invalidates kitabah is a condition that affects the essence of the contract. Hibah, sadaqah, nikah, khul', and sulh 'an dam al-'amd are not nullified by the exception of the unborn child; rather, the exception is nullified because these contracts are not nullified by invalid conditions. Similarly, wasiyyah is not nullified by it, but the exception is valid, so that the unborn child becomes inheritance and the slave-girl becomes a bequest, because wasiyyah is the sister of inheritance, and inheritance applies to what is in the womb. This is contrary to when he excepts her service, because inheritance does not apply to it. Commentary: The summary of the author of al-Hidayah's detail is that the contract in which an exception occurs has three types: (1) both contract and exception are fasid; (2) the contract is valid and the exception is void; (3) both contract and exception are valid. The first type is like sale, ijarah, kitabah, and rahn. For example, if someone sells his slave-girl but excludes her unborn child, or rents out his house and fixes its rent as a slave-girl but excludes her unborn child, or pawns his slave-girl but excludes her unborn child, or makes his slave a mukatab and fixes the kitabah price as a slave-girl but excludes her unborn child, in all these cases the contract becomes fasid because these contracts are nullified by invalid conditions, and they are nullified because besides sale, ijarah, kitabah, and rahn are in the meaning of sale due to being commutative contracts. Sale is nullified by invalid conditions, as previously explained, so contracts that are in the meaning of sale will also be nullified by invalid conditions. And making an exception is also permissible...
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the effect of excluding the unborn child (haml) from a sale of a slave-girl. The ruling is that the sale is fasid because the exception is invalid. The underlying principle is that anything that cannot be the sole subject of a contract cannot be excepted from it. The unborn child is considered like a part of the mother (similar to limbs), so it is included in the sale unless explicitly excepted; but such exception is contrary to the nature of the contract and becomes an invalid condition, nullifying the sale. Then the text distinguishes between different contracts. In hanafi fiqh, certain contracts (sale, ijarah, kitabah, rahn) are inherently commutative (mu'awada), and invalid conditions render them fasid. For other contracts (hibah, sadaqah, nikah, khul', sulh 'an dam al-'amd), invalid conditions do not nullify the contract; only the condition is void, but the contract remains valid. The text also explains the special case of wasiyyah (bequest): an exception of the unborn child is valid, so the unborn child inherits (as part of the estate) and the slave-girl becomes a bequest. This is because wasiyyah resembles inheritance, and inheritance includes what is in the womb. In contrast, excluding the service of the slave-girl does not affect inheritance. The passage concludes with a three-fold categorization of contracts regarding the exception of the unborn child, clarifying the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): The act of excluding something from the subject of a contract, e.g., excluding the unborn child from the sale of a slave-girl.
حمل (haml): The unborn child in the womb of a slave-girl; considered legally as part of the mother for purposes of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man sells his slave-girl but stipulates that her unborn child is not included. What is the ruling according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The sale is valid, and the child belongs to the seller.
B) The sale is fasid because the exception is an invalid condition.
C) The sale is valid, and the child belongs to the buyer by default.
D) The sale is batil due to uncertainty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an inseparable part of a sold item cannot be validly excepted; doing so in a commutative contract renders the contract fasid.
